## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations (dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching a second-order oscillator written as x' = v and v' = dv_dt = f(x,v,t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillator tasks commonly involve restoring forces (often nonlinear in x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly time-dependent forcing or parametric excitation via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, undamped/unforced)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Phase-shifted drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal forcing variant)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced oscillator)
- Pendulum (small-to-large angle restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear restoring from gravity, with damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation dominating at large |v|)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (nonlinear damping creating self-sustained oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (velocity-dependent negative damping at small |v|)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear potential gradient (general polynomial): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (restoring force from an even polynomial potential)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction + spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (smoothed sign(v) friction combined with viscous damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillator behavior often implies dv_dt depends primarily on x (dv_dt ≈ -dU/dx), with little/no explicit t or v dependence.
- Symmetric restoring forces for centered oscillators are typically odd in x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3, -sin(x)), producing symmetric trajectories about x=0.
- Hardening vs softening springs correspond to the sign of the x**3 term in dv_dt: negative coefficient on x**3 tends to harden (frequency increases with amplitude), positive tends to soften.
- Damping forces usually oppose motion, so terms involving v often enter as -v, -v*Abs(v), or other odd functions of v that remove energy over time.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles are suggested by state-dependent damping such as (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v, which injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing is typically represented by additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt, which can create resonance, quasiperiodicity, or chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance is suggested by time-varying stiffness multiplying x, e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, rather than additive forcing.
- Non-smooth frictional effects (stick–slip) manifest as sign-like dependencies on v; smooth approximations often use v/(Abs(v)+c) or tanh(c*v) to avoid discontinuities.
- Coupled nonlinear dissipation and restoring terms can create amplitude-dependent decay rates, where transient envelopes do not follow a single exponential and depend on initial conditions.

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Since x > 0 on this domain, |x| = x, so:
**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-x) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Simplifying:
**GT:** `0.273627*v³ - 0.332588*v - 0.111444*v*exp(-x) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³`
2. `v`
3. `v*exp(-x)`
4. `sin(t)`

Now let me examine what basis functions the candidates offer. The key issue is:
- **sin(t)**: None of the candidates contain `sin(t)`. They all use `exp(c*t)` instead.
- **v*exp(-x)**: Most candidates don't have this. Some have `v*x`, `v*x²`, `v*Abs(x)`, etc.

**Critical observation:** `exp(c*t)` can NEVER equal `sin(t)` for all t. These are linearly independent functions. `sin(t)` oscillates while `exp(c*t)` is monotonic (or constant if c=0). Setting c5=0 gives a constant, not sin(t). There is no way to make `exp(c*t)` match `sin(t)`.

Similarly, `v*exp(-x)` cannot be represented by `v*x`, `v*x²`, `1/x`, `x`, `Abs(v)`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v*log(...)`, or polynomial terms in x. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**For ALL candidates (1-50):**
- Every single candidate uses `exp(c*t)` for the time dependence, but the GT requires `sin(t)`. Since `exp(c*t)` and `sin(t)` are linearly independent functions, no value of constants can make `exp(c*t) = sin(t)` for all t ≥ 0.
- Additionally, the GT requires `v*exp(-x)`, which none of the candidates provide (they offer `v*x`, `v*x²`, `v*log(...)`, `v*Abs(x)`, or `exp(c*x)` without the v multiplier).

Since both `sin(t)` and `v*exp(-x)` are essential non-zero terms in the GT, and no candidate can reproduce either of these basis functions, none of the candidates can match.

Let me verify candidates 37 and 48 which have `exp(c*x)`:
- **Candidate 37:** Has `c3*exp(c4*x)` but not `v*exp(-x)`. Missing the `v` multiplier.
- **Candidate 48:** Has `c4*exp(c5*x)` but again not `v*exp(-x)`.

Both still use `exp(c*t)` instead of `sin(t)`.
